## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science - constitutive modeling of plastic deformation
**Analysis**: This task involves stress (sigma) as a function of strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), which is typical for modeling the mechanical response of materials under thermal activation. The relationship likely captures strain hardening (increasing stress with strain) and thermal softening (decreasing stress with temperature), common in solid mechanics and materials science.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hollomon strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (power-law relationship between true stress and true strain)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 - c1 * T (yield stress decreases linearly with temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) (stress decays exponentially with rising temperature)
- Combined Hollomon and thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (strain hardening with temperature-dependent flow stress)
- Temperature-dependent hardening exponent: sigma = c0 * epsilon**(c1 - c2 * T) (strain hardening exponent varies linearly with temperature)
- Saturation hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * exp(-c2 * T) (exponential approach to a saturation stress, scaled by temperature)
- Power-law hardening with additive temperature effect: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 + c2 * T + c3 (temperature shifts the stress additively)
- Polynomial interaction: sigma = c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*T + c3*epsilon*T (linear thermo-mechanical coupling)
- Ludwik hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (yield stress plus power-law hardening, softened exponentially by temperature)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(-c2 * T) (sine-hyperbolic relation for large strain ranges with temperature softening)
- Reciprocal temperature degradation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (c2 + T) (stress inversely related to absolute temperature level)
- Double power-law temperature effect: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T**c3) (temperature can also enhance stress through rate-dependent mechanisms)
- Exponential strain hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * epsilon) * exp(-c2 * T) (log-linear hardening at low strains)
- Voce saturation hardening: sigma = c0 - (c0 - c1) * exp(-c2 * epsilon) (saturation stress c0, initial yield c1; temperature can parameterize c0, c1, c2)
- Yield strength threshold with hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1*T) + c2 * epsilon**c3 (temperature‐dependent yield stress plus strain hardening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening → Power-law dependence (epsilon**n) with exponent between 0 and 1
- Thermal softening → Negative exponential or negative linear dependence on temperature (exp(-c*T) or -c*T)
- Saturation of flow stress → Exponential approach to a limit (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Yield stress as initial threshold → Additive constant term (c0) independent of strain
- Temperature-modulated hardening exponent → Exponent containing linear term in T (epsilon**(c1 + c2*T))
- Thermo-mechanical coupling → Multiplicative term epsilon * T or epsilon**n * f(T)
- Inverse temperature dependence → Stress ∝ 1/(c + T), hyperbolic sensitivity to temperature
- High-strain linear hardening → Linear term in epsilon at large strains (c1*epsilon) plus power-law saturation
- Rate-independent plasticity → Stress expressed purely as function of strain and temperature without strain rate arguments
